Date:  Sat, 09 Jan 2016 17:15:33 +0000
From:  Damian Peach 
Subject:  Comet 67P - Jan 8th
Hi all,
Here is an image of 67P taken yesterday using a large aperture telescope.
The tail has changed allot since my last image in early December. It is now bifurcated with two faint streamers and extends out of the frame with a notable large kink in it toward bottom right. Also a faint forward pointing anti-tail like feature is present.
http://www.damianpeach.com/deepsky/67p_2016_01_08dp.jpg
27"CDK with FLI CCD. LRGB. 25/3/3/3mins.

Best Wishes
Damian

Date:  Thu, 14 Jan 2016 13:53:38 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Another anomalous tail for c/2013 US10?
Comet Catalina from this morning at ASO; the only reason that I am posting here is
that there appears to be a 3rd anomalous tail in addition to the gas and dust tail
which are still prevalent.
All .fits images are showing this possible third component, seen in this photo (no
post processing, just saved as a .jpg) in about an 8:00 clock position relative to
the coma.
Photo and discussion posted at Arkansas Sky Observatories:
http://www.arksky.org/smf/index.php/topic,2706.0.html

From:  Damian Peach 
Subject:  67P in the Virgo cluster - Jan 18th
Hi all,
Here is an image of 67P on the outskirts of the Virgo cluster. The large elliptical galaxy in shot is NGC 4365, though many other galaxies are visible in the field. The edge on galaxy with dark bisecting dust lane nearby is NGC 4370.
http://www.damianpeach.com/deepsky/67p_2016_01_18dp.jpg
20"CDK with FLI camera. LRGB. 40/5/5/5min.

Date:  Fri, 22 Jan 2016 22:18:25 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2013 US10 Catalina (Jan.11,2016)
Object/Date:C/2013 US10 (Catalina) @ Jan.11,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) imaged on January 11th 2016. Since my last image on December has evolved increasing the size of tail formed by heavy particles that revolve toward southwest (toward down left in the image) once come off from comet nucleus which has surrounded by a gassy coma of intense bluish color. The ionic tail is directed toward west (at right) with more than 5 degrees long and getting out of the image, although is more faint that on past days, is showing several knots and structures. Between all galaxies which can be observed, stands out NGC 5371 in the middle of image.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M 2x(L:2×240s + RGB:1x60s Bin2)
Location:Remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013us10-catalina-20160111/
Regards.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

On Saturday, January 23, 2016 5:18 AM, "José J. Chambó jjchambo@hotmail.com [Comet-Images]" wrote:

Object/Date:C/2013 US10 (Catalina) @ Jan.11,2016Description:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) imaged on January 11th 2016. Since my last image on December has evolved increasing the size of tail formed by heavy particles that revolve toward southwest (toward down left in the image) once come off from comet nucleus which has surrounded by a gassy coma of intense bluish color. The ionic tail is directed toward west (at right) with more than 5 degrees long and getting out of the image, although is more faint that on past days, is showing several knots and structures. Between all galaxies which can be observed, stands out NGC 5371 in the middle of image.Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M 2x(L:2×240s + RGB:1x60s Bin2)Location:Remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013us10-catalina-20160111/Regards.José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Tue, 26 Jan 2016 19:57:54 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2013 X1 PANSTARRS (Dec.30)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) @ Dec.30,2015
Description:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) imaged on December 30th, 2015 a few days after start a fast increase of activity. In this image show a brightness near magnitude 9, developing a gassy coma with a diameter of 7 minutes and a tail with at least 15 minutes of longitude towards northeast.
Location:Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain) Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (1x240s ISO-1600)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013x1-panstarrs-20151230/

Regards.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo 

Date:  Thu, 28 Jan 2016 12:13:45 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  c2015 X8 NEOWISE
A quick note and request for observations on comet c/2015 X8 NEOWISE; about 10 days
ago we logged the comet as conspicuous although irregular and diffuse at mag. 17.2
(m2); last night (Jan 28 UT) the comet could barely be found, a very large and
scattered diffuse cloud centered on the position of where the comet's core should be.
Very difficult and almost transparent; we assigned a magnitude (m2) of 18.9 or 19.0
which is conservatively brighter than the nucleus actually appeared. Observations are
highly recommend for what appears to be a disintegrating comet.

------------
Dr. Clay

Arkansas Sky Observatories
WEB: http://www.arksky.org/
FACEBOOK: https://www.facebook.com/groups/421163751426836/
ASO Petit Jean Mountain /MPC H41
ASO Petit Jean Mountain South /MPC H45
ASO West Conway /MPC H43
.......serving astronomy since 1971

Description:Comet C/2015 V2 (Johnson) imaged on December 30th, 2015 seven weeks after the image which I have taken later its discovery, now seems has increased its brightness from magnitude 17 to 16. This comet could be observable with small binoculars on mid 2017.

Subject:  C/2013 X1 PanSTARRS January 6, 2013, A Day after The Onset of Outburst
There look to be two tails, longer bluish tail and shorter yellowish tail a bit to the north. The bluish tail was long, more than two degrees at the night. North is up.

Date:  Tue, 02 Feb 2016 10:56:40 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2013 X1 PANSTARRS (Jan.9)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) @ Jan.9,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) imaged on January 9th, 2016 just at its maximum of an outburst which began at the end of December when was in magnitude 10 and ended in this image with a brightness of magnitude 8, with a coma of 11 arcminutes of diameter and a faint tail toward northeast.
Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (8x120s ISO-800, cropped) from Vallés, Valencia (Spain)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013x1-panstarrs-20160109/

Date:  Thu, 04 Feb 2016 09:43:21 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet Catalina & Whirlpool Galaxy
Object/Date:C/2013 US10 (Catalina) @ Jan.13,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) imaged on January 13th 2016 in a wide field. Its long ionic tail is projected toward west to a distance of more than 6 degrees, but more faint and with less details that in my previous image taken only two days ago; however the dust tail more short and brilliant toward south barely changed. Aside from several small galaxies scattered by field, in the upper right highlights the classical spiral galaxy M 51: the Whirlpool Galaxy.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M, mosaic 3x(L:2×300s + RGB:1x60s Bin2) remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013us10-catalina-20160113/

Clear Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Sat, 06 Feb 2016 01:18:47 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet C/2013 US10 Catalina (Jan.17)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) @ Jan.17,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) imaged on January 17th, 2016 in a nice conjunction with the Pinwheel Galaxy (M 101) at left, and the pair of stars most popular in boreal skies, Mizar and Alcor, at upper right. The comet shows its dust tail toward down, whereas that a very faint ionic tail is barely visible projected toward the quoted couple of stars.
Tech data:Canon EFS 18-135 at 116mm. f/5.6 & Canon EOS-100D (3x480s ISO-1600, cropped) from Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013us10-catalina-20160117a/

Clear Skies.

Date:  Tue, 09 Feb 2016 01:17:23 -0000
From:  Peter Carson 
Subject:  P/2010V1 Ikeya-Murakami
Hi All,
I secured an image of P/2010V1 tonight in amongst the passing cloud from my urban observatory here in SE Essex UK. I managed 68 minutes of exposure which was long enough to record the debris field of fragment B, although it was too faint and diffuse to measure. Fragment C is the brightest, measured at mag 18.1. P/2010V1A was unfortunately too close to a star to measure it. Couldn’t see any evidence of any other fragment.
Image attached.

Peter Carson

Date:  Sat, 13 Feb 2016 15:22:07 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Catalina US10 Finally clears the OTY roof!
Hello All,

One of my blind spots at our observatory here in Payson is due north - the direction the roll off roof goes when pushed back. The comet has finally after several weeks cleared the roofs peak, and I can now once again image this fading space wanderer. This image was taken a few days ago, and reveals the 7th magnitude object to still have a sizeable dust tail, and a weak pale blue gas tail. The new 10" seems to give the right sized field for this object, here spanning around 1.5 degrees in width.

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/CatalinaUS1-021116.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

Date:  Wed, 17 Feb 2016 03:29:56 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet 67P - Churyumov Gerasimenko on 2/14
Hello all,

This newly competed image taken a few days ago was examined on at least 6 different monitors both CRT and LCD to make sure I didnt have colored noise all over the image. The problem is pretty common - you process on a CRT and when viewed with an LCD the colors are harsh and noisy because the limited number of grey shades. Until I get a new monitor this week, Ill just have to test the images on multiple computers before posting! Thanks to Jose for pointing this flaw out to me....

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/CometCG021416.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

Date:  Wed, 24 Feb 2016 12:48:00 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet C/2013 US10 Catalina (Jan.17)
A delayed image:
Object/Date:C/2013 US10 (Catalina) @ Jan.17,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) imaged on January 17th 2016, in conjunction with the Pinwheel Galaxy (M 101) at left, and the popular pair of stars Mizar and Alcor surrounded by a bright halo induced by the refractor telescope optics. The comet stands out in center with its greenish coma from which departs a bright dust tail arched toward down, and a long ionic tail more faint toward right, going above the couple of stars.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M, mosaic 3x(L:2×240s + RGB:1x60s Bin2) remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013us10-catalina-20160117b/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Fri, 04 Mar 2016 20:08:51 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comets 252P/LINEAR & P/2016 BA14 (Mar.2)
Object/Date:252P/LINEAR & P/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) @ Mar.2,2016
Description:Comets 252P/LINEAR and P/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) imaged on March 2nd 2016, separated by only 1.5 degrees seem very differents: the 252P with a enormous and greenish gassy envelope while the 2016-BA14 is just a tiny mote between stars, nonetheless the similitude of its orbits seem reveal that really are fragments of a unique comet. Both are approaching to Earth, being its minimum distance 0.0036 and 0.0016 AU between March 21 and 22 (14 and 9 times the lunar distance). Between comets can be viewed the spiral galaxy NGC 2090.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:2×240s bin1 + RGB:1x60s Bin2, cropped) remotely from Siding Spring,
NSW (Australia)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2-cometas-hermanos/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Object/Date:

252P/LINEAR & P/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) @ Mar.2,2016

Description:

Comets 252P/LINEAR and P/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) imaged on March 2nd 2016,
separated by only 1.5 degrees seem very differents: the 252P with a enormous
and greenish gassy envelope while the 2016-BA14 is just a tiny mote between
stars, nonetheless the similitude of its orbits seem reveal that really are
fragments of a unique comet. Both are approaching to Earth, being its
minimum distance 0.0036 and 0.0016 AU between March 21 and 22 (14 and 9
times the lunar distance). Between comets can be viewed the spiral galaxy
NGC 2090.

Tech data:

Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:2×240s bin1 + RGB:1x60s
Bin2, cropped) remotely from Siding Spring,

NSW (Australia)

Date:  Fri, 04 Mar 2016 23:06:44 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  RE: Comets 252P/LINEAR & P/2016 BA14 (Mar.2)
I apologize, there are a mistake in the minimum distances to Earth in A.U., the correct description is:
Comets 252P/LINEAR and P/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) imaged on March 2nd 2016, separated by only 1.5 degrees seem very differents: the 252P with a enormous and greenish gassy envelope while the 2016-BA14 is just a tiny mote between stars, nonetheless the similitude of its orbits seem reveal that really are fragments of a unique comet. Both are approaching to Earth, being its minimum distance 0.036 and 0.024 AU between March 21 and 22 (14 and 9 times the lunar distance). Between comets can be viewed the spiral galaxy NGC 2090.

José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

From: jjchambo@hotmail.com
To: comet-images@yahoogroups.com; comets-ml@yahoogroups.com
Subject: Comets 252P/LINEAR & P/2016 BA14 (Mar.2)
Date: Fri, 4 Mar 2016 20:08:51 +0100

Object/Date:252P/LINEAR & P/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) @ Mar.2,2016
Description:Comets 252P/LINEAR and P/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) imaged on March 2nd 2016, separated by only 1.5 degrees seem very differents: the 252P with a enormous and greenish gassy envelope while the 2016-BA14 is just a tiny mote between stars, nonetheless the similitude of its orbits seem reveal that really are fragments of a unique comet. Both are approaching to Earth, being its minimum distance 0.0036 and 0.0016 AU between March 21 and 22 (14 and 9 times the lunar distance). Between comets can be viewed the spiral galaxy NGC 2090.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:2×240s bin1 + RGB:1x60s Bin2, cropped) remotely from Siding Spring,
NSW (Australia)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2-cometas-hermanos/

Date:  Thu, 17 Mar 2016 12:52:54 -0500
From:  Ignacio Ferrin 
Subject:  Re: [comets-ml] P/2016 BA14: an image (16 Mar. 2016)
Hello all:

The image by Gianluca is rather interesting. I can not discern any
coma around the object in a negative image using MAXIM-DL.
The profile is stellar. It seems to be a bare nucleus. That is
rather strange if this is a fragment of 252P. Or perhaps it was
active some time ago and now all ice has been consumed. More
images are needed in the coming days to see if a very faint coma
has remained.

Ignacio

Date:  Sat, 19 Mar 2016 21:51:01 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) @ Mar.6,2016
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) @ Mar.6,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 US10 (PANSTARRS) on March 6th 2016, has moved away to 2 A.U. from the Sun and Earth, showing a lot of changes since the last time I shoot near two months ago: its brightness has dropped to magnitude 9.5, its gas tail has missed, and the dust tail with a longitude of half degree has been stretched because our perspective as the Earth approaches to its orbital plane.
Location:Vallés, Valencia (Spain) Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (6x240s ISO-1600)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013us10-catalina-20160306/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Mon, 21 Mar 2016 21:52:20 -0000
From:  Peter Carson 
Subject:  Comet 2016BA14 PanSTARRS this evening
Hi All,
The clouds cleared here in Essex allowing me to image this fast moving comet.
I’ve put an animation of 23 x 20 second exposures is on Youtube https://youtu.be/NT6AywxHrnk
A stack of the exposures can be seen here http://www.astromania.co.uk/2016BA14_20160321_2021_PCarson.jpg
No coma was recorded, but the nearly full Moon was very nearby, washing out the sky.
Regards
Peter Carson

Date:  Thu, 24 Mar 2016 18:09:16 +0100
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2015 V2 (Johnson) @ Mar.6,2016
Object/Date:Comet C/2015 V2 (Johnson) @ Mar.6,2016
Description:Comet C/2015 V2 (Johnson) imaged on March 6th 2016. With a magnitude near the 16th by comparing with the stars of around, seems show some greenish tone which could mean a gassy activity when it is to 5.4 AU from Sun yet. When reach its perihelion on July 2017 this comet could be observable with binoculars.
Location:Vallés, Valencia (Spain) Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (10 x 240 sec. at ISO-800)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2015v2-johnson-20160306/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Fri, 01 Apr 2016 23:49:34 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2014 S2 (PANSTARRS) @ Mar.8,2016
Object/Date:Comet C/2014 S2 (PANSTARRS) @ Mar.8,2016
Description:Comet C/2014 S2 (PANSTARRS) imaged on March 8th 2016, with a brightness around magnitude 9.5 and a coma of 5' diameter everytime more white, shows a short dust tail towards southeast (to down-right) a a faint anti-tail towards north (upwards) because the approximation of Earth to its orbital plane.
Location:Vallés, Valencia (Spain) Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (4 x 240 sec. at ISO-800)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2014s2-panstarrs-20160308/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Sat, 02 Apr 2016 16:36:00 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Linear 252P this morning - A sizeable object!
Hello all,

Clouds finally parted with us here in Arizona this morning after weeks of very poor high clouds and rain. I hemmed and hawed about which scope to use, since this comet is so big in angular size. I finally settled on using the Cometraker 6" f/3.6 Astrograph because of its flat field and large 2 x 3 degree coverage. :

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/Linear252P-040216.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

Date:  Sun, 03 Apr 2016 12:49:23 -0400
From:  Joe Stieber 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 252P LRGB April 3
Michael,

An excellent image!

I see a slightly brighter streak in the coma, extending to the right of the
central condensation (it's more apparent if I move back from the screen a
bit). Is that a tail?

Looking at 252P on a SkyTools chart for 02:45 UT on April 3, the direction
of the streak with respect to the field stars in the image matches the
direction of the tail line on the SkyTools comet symbol (which is in the
anti-solar direction).

Joe Stieber

Date:  Tue, 05 Apr 2016 17:50:34 +0100
From:  Peter Carson 
Subject:  Comet 252P from urban SE Essex UK
I managed my first image of 252P Linear last night from my rather light polluted observatory here in SE Essex UK. The comet had not long risen so was rather poorly placed, I should have imaged it later in the night when it was higher but the weather was closing in.
The coma is very large but from my light polluted location its difficult to record it faithfully. My attempt can be seen here http://www.astromania.co.uk/252P_20160405_0059_PCarson.jpg
Peter Carson
http://www.astromania.co.uk/comets.htm

Date:  Wed, 06 Apr 2016 15:16:59 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image 252P/LINEAR (Apr. 5, 2016)
Object/Date:252P/LINEAR @ Abr.5,2016
Description:After approaching to 0.036 AU to Earth, the comet 252P/LINEAR has had an outburst that have triggered an oversized coma of 1 degree and has increased its brightness until magnitude 6, being observable at naked eye from dark skies. When was taken this image on April 5th, 2106 the comet passed close to M14, a globular cluster on the Milky Way in the constellation Ophiuchus.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:4×240s,bin1 + RGB:1x60s,Bin2) remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/252p-linear-20160405/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Thu, 07 Apr 2016 16:11:24 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image/Video C/2016 BA14 PANSTARRS (Mar.27,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) @ Mar.27,2016
Description:Comet C/2016 BA14 (PANSTARRS) imaged on March 27 2016, five days after its maximum approaching to Earth. In spite of be presumed a fragment of the comet 252P/LINEAR who shows these days a big and gassy coma, the 2016-BA14 seems have an asteroid shape. Only after stack a lot of frames by means of a rejection algorithm and overprocessing the resulting image, can be seen a vague tail toward southwest (toward down right).
GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (210 x 45 sec. at ISO-1600), from Vallés, Valencia (Spain)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2016ba14-panstarrs-20160327/
A video with all frames:
https://vimeo.com/161900545

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Fri, 15 Apr 2016 00:47:08 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2014 S2 PANSTARRS (Apr.9,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2014 S2 (PANSTARRS) @ Apr.9,2016
Description:Comet C/2014 S2 (PANSTARRS) imaged on April 9 2016, with a brightness of magnitude 10 and a coma of 5' diameter, the comet still showing a twin dust tail because to closeness of Earth to its orbital plane: the thrown tail (type II) of 15' toward southeast and the trail tail (type III) of 7' toward north.
Location:Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain) Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (3 x 240 sec. at ISO-1600)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2014s2-panstarrs-20160409/
Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Over the past couple of days I have tried to image that comet but this

Date:  Wed, 20 Apr 2016 11:55:38 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2013 US10 Catalina (Apr.9,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) @ Apr.9,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 US10 (Catalina) imaged on April 9 2016, even though its brightness has dropped to magnitude 11, photographically still has a nice look with a coma of 3' diameter and a narrow dust tail of 0.5 degrees long. Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (7 x 240 sec. at ISO-1600) from Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013us10-catalina-20160409/

Dark Skies.

From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Panstarrs S2 - May 4th - A VERY nice comet indeed!
Hello All,

Clear skies returned to Arizona once again for a day or two and this new image shows two very fine tail extensions from the inner coma. I was surprised to see that both the fan and more straighter tail both were cyan/teal colored on the RGB data. Still, the comet is progressing structurally very nicely!

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/PanstarrsS2-050416.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Date:  Fri, 13 May 2016 09:08:32 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2013 X1 PANSTARRS (May.11,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) @ May.11,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) imaged on May 11 2016, in spite of bad weather when I took the image with high humidity and poor transparency, is possible see its two tails: the dust tail toward up left with more than half degree, and the ion tail toward down right which showing several jets in its begining, and although faint is prolonged al least a pair of degrees until the bright star Phi Aquarii with magnitude 4. The comet has a brightness of magnitude 7 and will be increasing next days because is approaching to Earth.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:4×240s bin1 + RGB:1x60s Bin2, cropped) remotely from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013x1-panstarrs-20160511/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Tue, 17 May 2016 09:26:15 +0000
From:  denis buczynski 
Subject:  Latest edition of BAA The Comet's Tale
A new edition of the section's newsletter, The Comet's Tale, is now
available for download from the BAA website here:

https://britastro.org/pdf/CometSection/tail35.pdf

This is the first edition produced under my directorship and I would
like to thank all of the contributors and, in particular, the editor,
Janice McClean. I hope you enjoy reading it. Feedback is welcome, as are
any offers of articles for future editions!

An archive of previous editions going back to 1995 is available on the
Comet Section website here:

https://britastro.org/node/6812

Nick James. Comet Section Director.

Date:  Thu, 19 May 2016 12:53:14 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image 252P/LINEAR (May 16,2016)
Object/Date:Comet 252P/LINEAR @ May 16,2016
Description:Comet 252P/LINEAR imaged on May 16 2016, since my last image taken one month ago the comet is now 8 times less brilliant, from magnitude 6 to 9, in the same way that its fuzzy greenish coma has decreased from a diameter of 45 to only 10 arcminutes.
Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (10 x 120 sec. at ISO-1600); from Vallés, Valencia (Spain)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/252p-linear-20160516/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo 

Date:  Fri, 20 May 2016 16:31:22 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2013 X1 PANSTARRS (May 18,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) @ May 18,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) in a wide field image taken on May 11 2016, shows toward left a dust trail (tail type III) with half degree of length that remaining in its orbit, and a long ionic tail (type I) very faint which is projected with more than three degrees long toward down-right of the image. The comet is located into constellation Aquarius and is observable through binoculars before dawn.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:4×240 sec. bin1 + RGB:1x120 sec. Bin2, cropped) remotely from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013x1-panstarrs-20160518/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo 

Date:  Tue, 24 May 2016 11:21:57 -0700
From:  michaeljaeger@gmx.at
Subject:  Ten years ago
Dear colleagues

Ten years ago, more than 60 fragments of comet 73P were observed.
The fragments B and C were close together end of May.
The newly revised images of 25 and 28 May show the twin comets.
Image were made with Leica Apo 180/f-3.4 and FLI MaxCam3200 at Tivoli/Namibia.

Best Regards
Michael Jäger

May 25

http://spaceweathergallery.com/indiv_upload.php?upload_id=126017 http://spaceweathergallery.com/indiv_upload.php?upload_id=126017

large

http://spaceweathergallery.com/full_image.php?image_name=michael-jAcger-73PBC20060525lrgbv100-Kopie1111_1464113324.jpg http://spaceweathergallery.com/full_image.php?image_name=michael-jAcger-73PBC20060525lrgbv100-Kopie1111_1464113324.jpg

May 28

http://spaceweathergallery.com/full_image.php?image_name=michael-jAcger-73PBCmay28newweb_1464113324.jpg http://spaceweathergallery.com/full_image.php?image_name=michael-jAcger-73PBCmay28newweb_1464113324.jpg

Date:  Thu, 09 Jun 2016 17:10:01 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2014 S2 PANSTARRS (Jun.3,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2014 S2 (PANSTARRS) @ Jun.3,2016
Description:Comet C/2014 S2 (PANSTARRS) imaged on June 3 2016 when its brightness has dropped until near magnitude 12. Likewise its look has waned since the last image I took two months ago: coma has been reduced to only 2 arcminutes, and the dust tails have merged in a small fan that opens from East to North.
Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (4 x 240 sec. at ISO-1600); from Navas de Estena, Ciudad Real (Spain)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2014s2-panstarrs-20160603/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Sun, 12 Jun 2016 21:48:14 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image 252P/LINEAR (Jun.4,2016)
Object/Date:Comet 252P/LINEAR @ Jun.4,2016
Description:Comet 252P/LINEAR imaged on June 4 2016, just when begins a fast drop in brightness. In this image is near magnitude 11.5 and can be perceived as, comparing with the image I took three weeks before in which had magnitude 9, the central condensation has lost intensity and the coma has dimmed in diameter from 10 to 3 arcminutes.
Tech data:GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (11 x 240 sec. at ISO-1600); from Navas de Estena, Ciudad Real (Spain)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/252p-linear-20160604/

Date:  Tue, 14 Jun 2016 21:13:54 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2013 X1 PANSTARRS (Jun.12,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) @ June 12,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) imaged on June 12 2016, only 10 days before its maximum approach to Earth with a brightness near magnitude 6.5 is observable through binoculars. In this wide field image highlights a greenish coma with an appearent diameter as big as the Moon, from its departs toward upper left a dust trail (type III) with more than a degree long, also can be viewed a long and narrow ionic tail very faint towards right. As novelty aso can be observed the begin of its classical dust tail (type II) projected only a few arcminutes towards upper right. The brishtest star of the field is Iota Piscis Austrini with magnitude 4, and also can be perceived near the down right corner a small and faint interstellar cloud associated to infrared emission source IRAS F21276-3327.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:3×180s bin1 + RGB:1x60s Bin2) remotely from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013x1-panstarrs-20160612/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Thu, 16 Jun 2016 18:17:01 +0000
From:  denis buczynski 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 2013X1_16 06 disconnection event
Gerald,This is a comet image to take the breath away. Superb. How lucky we are that the technical processes of comet imaging have reached this level. Looking back at the history of comet photography, even images taken with the big schmidt telescopes rarely showed this amount of detail. Obviously the excellent observatory location is crucial to the quality of the final image, and you have had the commitment to place your set up there for that reason. You deserve the successes you constantly achieve. Well done. Post more images of this event. One in colour would be spectacular.Best wishesDenis BuczynskiBAA Comet Section

Date:  Tue, 05 Jul 2016 15:00:15 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2013 X1 PANSTARRS (Jun.30,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) @ June 30,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) imaged on June 30 2016, a week after its maximum approach to Earth and moving away toward outer of Solar System, the comet suddenly has lost its ion tail, remaining only the dust trail behind its orbit (tail type III). In this wide field image the comet appears above a dense zone of the Milky Way between constellations Scorpius and Ara with its tail projected towards the globular cluster NGC 6352. The brightest star at upper is Iota Arae and down-left can be perceived the glow of the near star Alpha Arae of magnitude 2.8.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:3×120s bin1 + RGB:1x60s Bin2) remotely from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013x1-panstarrs-20160630/

Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Thu, 28 Jul 2016 15:02:21 +0200
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2013 X1 PANSTARRS (Jul.25,2016)
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) @ July 25,2016
Description:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) imaged on July 25 2016, shows these days a tail formed for a narrow and long trail of dust very sharp because our planet is intersecting the orbital plane of the comet and we see edgeways its projection of dust particles which are spread at same plane. Its head highlights with a strong greenish color due to emission of C2 molecules.
In this widefield image the tail have more than a degree long (two times the apparent diameter of the full moon) until is mixed into the glow of a beautiful couple of bright stars which contrast its colors in the constellation Centaurus, at right the redish C01 with magnitude 4 and at left the bluish C02 with magnitude 5.
Tech data:Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:4×180s bin1 + RGB:1x120s Bin2) cropped, from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013x1-panstarrs-20160725/

Clear & Dark Skies.
José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Just a few friendly suggestions on the new layout.

1. Have the latest image at the top of the image list so srcolling to the bottom and waiting for the bottom thumbnails to load is not necessary.

2. Automatically display the latest (topmost) image.

I really liked the older layout where you could click on the image list, look at the image, and then click on the image to return to the image list. Very slick.

But I guess things change for the better.

I always enjoy your posts and keep up the great work.

Dave

Date:  Sun, 04 Sep 2016 22:35:47 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet SW1 Last night - 090316
HI all,

The 12.5" newtonian is back together again, and with freshly re coated mirrors is now starting to bang out some comet images again! So exciting to get the scope in operation again. This is first light for the new mirror coatings. I had some of the aperture occulted by the observatory wall, since this comet is pretty darn low in the south. So I probably shot this with a six inch. ;)

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/ccdimagepages/cometsw1-090316.html

Wouldnt you know that the comet had an major upsurge in brightness while the mirror was in the shop! Oh well...

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Image C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) 26-Aug
Object/Date:Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) @ August 26,2016
Comet C/2013 X1 (PANSTARRS) was visible with binoculars a few months ago. Imaged here on August 26 2016 when is definitively moving out from inside Solar System losing fast its brightness, in spite of which this image taken with a high sensibility remote equipment from Siding Spring Observatories complex in Australia, achieves to show its faint dust trail extending with 1 degree long (as two full moons) departing from its head green tinted due to emission of carbonic gas.
Aside from several tiny galaxies scattered by the field, at right bottom highlights the galaxy NGC 5556 type spiral barred that was discovered by John Herschel in 1834.
ASA Astrograph 16" N 406mm. f/3.5 & Apogee Aspen CG16070 (L:3×180s Bin1 + RGB:1x60s Bin2) cropped; from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia)
Post and image link:http://cometografia.es/2013x1-panstarrs-20160826/

Clear skies.

José J. Chambó (Valencia, Spain)blog: cometografia.es twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Fri, 07 Oct 2016 19:07:35 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Encke Last night - In color, no dust trail...
HI all,

With over an hour exposure, I had hoped to get this comets dust trail however it was not to be.  I did indeed capture the comet in exactly the position that Megastar plotted it for that hour.  Need less to say I stretched the hell out of the L frame and was only able to bring up a star flare (lower right) and an unidentified asteroid.  Oh well, hordes of galaxies anyway!

Anyone want to take a shot at what asteroid this is?

Date:  Fri, 21 Oct 2016 19:53:35 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Spacewatch KP36 Last night
Hello All,

Back to comet imaging now that the excruciatingly long Arizona monsoon is finally over with. Last night we captured this gem, an very peculiar shaped coma and hints of a tail on this 14th magnitude denizen of Cetus. In color, of course!

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/spacewatchKP36-102016.html

So many galaxies in Cetus in the background. One hour exposure with my 10 inch gets me a solid 19th magnitude for galaxies. There is an asteroid labeled with an "A" in this image, but must be a number over 5000 since it was not in the Cartes data base. Anyone know either how to add all the larger numbered asteroids or perhaps an onine data base that identifies the errant rock?

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

Date:  Thu, 27 Oct 2016 18:53:28 -0700
From:  tpolakis@cox.net
Subject:  Re: Comet Spacewatch KP36 Last night
Hi Chris,

Nice image. Regarding the asteroid on your image, believe it or not, the SkySafari app does a good job with identifying them. It shows (13817) Genobechetti at that position (00 37 42, -03 45 50) on 2016 Oct 21.15, which is the time of your image. It reports a magnitude of 17.9.

Another identification method involves using the Minor Planet Checker at the MPC site. It shows that asteroid at the same position, and gives a V magnitude of 17.3.

Tom

Date:  Sun, 30 Oct 2016 20:22:57 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  174P/Echeclus (Sep.4,2016)
A delayed image...

Object/Date:
Comet 174P/Echeclus @ Sep.4,2016

Description:
Comet 174P/Echeclus imaged on 2016 September 4th, during its last outburst. Discovered in 2000 was classified as an asteroid Centaur type circulating between orbits of Uranus and Jupiter, but years later it showed cometary activity with outbursts in 2006, 2011 and the present in 2016, in which increased from 17.5 to 14.5 magnitude. In the image can be perceive a tiny elongated coma of 20 arcseconds toward Northwest.

Tech data:
GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D unmodded (3 x 300 sec. at ISO-1600) from Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/174p-echeclus-20160904/

Clear Skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

Date:  Wed, 23 Nov 2016 12:57:04 -0800
From:  michaeljaeger@gmx.at
Subject:  C/2016 U1 near NGC4088
Hello

Comet Neowise is a small gas comet. On the morning of the 23rd of November he appeared very diffuse, with very weak condensation, on single image. The sum image shows a 5 'coma. The total brightness is currently 13m0. The central condensation is only 18mag. It is possible that the comet is brighter than 10 mag in one month.

Best Regards
Michael Jäger

nov. 23. 1.01 UT 10x170sec 12"/f-4

Date:  Sun, 27 Nov 2016 20:34:19 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  43P/Wolf-Harrington @ October 11,2016)
Object/Date:
43P/Wolf-Harrington @ October 11,2016

Description:
Comet 43P/Wolf-Harrington had an outburst at the end of August 2016, some days after pass its perihelion, increasing brightness until magnitude 11. In this image taken on October 11th 2016 the comet have dropped its luminosity until magnitude 12.5 still showing a dust tail with a long at least of 15 arcminutes.

Tech data:
Planewave 20" CDK 2280mm f/4.5 & FLI-PL11002M (L:2×120s + RGB:1x60s Bin2) remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/43p-wolf-harrington-20161011/



Clear Skies.

Date:  Fri, 02 Dec 2016 11:56:41 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2016 U1 (NEOWISE) & C/2015 V2 (Johnson) @ December 1,2016
Object/Date:
Comets C/2016 U1 (NEOWISE) & C/2015 V2 (Johnson) @ December 1,2016

Description:
Two new comets in approach to Sun casually concur into same field near Whirlpool Galaxy (M 51) in this image taken on December 1st, 2016. At the left bottom, the recently discovered C/2016 U1 (NEOWISE) shows a fuzzy and green coma due to its composing of ionized carbonic gas, while at upper right is the comet C/2015 V2 (Johnson) with very different morphology, more dusty that gassy, shows a small and whitis coma from which departs a short tail of dust. Both comets could be observed using binoculars in the future: NEOWISE at the end of this month of December before immerse into light of dawn, of which perhaps will not come out because is possible the comet to disintegrate at approach to Sun; comet Johnson will reach its maximum brightness on next spring 2017.

Tech data:
Takahashi FSQ ED 106mm. f/5.0 & SBIG STL-11000M (L:3×180s bin1 + RGB:1x60s Bin2) remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016u1-neowise-2015v2-johnson-20161201/

Clear and Dark Skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: facebook.com/JoseJChambo

Date:  Fri, 09 Dec 2016 19:58:27 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet C/2015 V2 Johnson this morning
HI all,

this is turning out to be really a beautiful object for the CCD. Getting up at 3am in the winter and rolling back the observatory roof for shooting is never fun, but such a nice tail got me going. Although the last third of the images were too faded to use because the secondary mirror frosted over, I still had 8 good 3 min subs and the RGB data to work with.

This is the first time in a year I was able to image a comet with the newly re coated mirror on the 12.5", and I was thrilled to see I had gotten over a magnitude and a half fainter than the equivelent exposure with the 10 inch. Ive posted my results here. Thanks for looking:

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/cometJohnson120916.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

Date:  Sun, 18 Dec 2016 22:44:32 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Four faint comets last night
Hi all,

2P Encke, C/2015 VL62 Lemmon-Yeung-Panstarrs, 93P Lovas 1, C/2011 KP36 Spacewatch

Freezing ice all over everything last night, i got in four new comet shots before the 12.5" frosted over! Interesting that Lovas 1 has a nice short stubby tail.

Comet images on this page, with photo keys showing faint galaxies too:

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/Fourcomets121716.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

Date:  Sun, 25 Dec 2016 19:43:34 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  45P/Honda-Mrkos-Pajdusakova  @ Dec.23,2016
Object/Date:
Comet 45P/Honda-Mrkos-Pajdusakova @ Dec.23,2016

Description:
Comet 45P/Honda-Mrkos-Pajdusakova imaged on December 23, 2016 in your way toward perihelion, few days after begining to develop a long ionic tail with several degrees long which exits from image field toward East. Although the comet is only at 8 degrees of altitude from horizon, doing hard the photography, can be seen that really is a twin tail departing from the greenish coma of comet, which shining near magnitude 8 being observable with binoculars.
Tech data:
GSO 8" f/3.8 & Canon EOS-100D (7 x 120 sec. at ISO-1600) from Benali, Valencia (Spain)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/45p-honda-mrkos-pajdusakova-20161223/

Clear and Dark Skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: facebook.com/JoseJChambo
